Reinforced fill materials should be placed in level loose lifts not exceeding
8 inches in loose thickness and be compacted to at least 95 percent of the
maximum dry density established in accordance with AASHTO T 180 Test
Methods at moisture contents above the optimum
3 9 Steepened Cut Slopes
We understand that the realigned Hoomana Road will require cut slopes on both
sides of the new alignment Based on the information provided cut slope heights of up to
about 40 feet will be required to achieve design grades As mentioned previously a cut
slope inclination of 2H 1V or flatter may be used for the design of the planned cut slopes
exposing medium stiff to very stiff residual soils and saprolite However due to the
limited right of way of the new Hoomana Road we understand that it is desired to
construct a steeper cut slope to accommodate the elevation difference Based on the
relatively high cut slope planned we recommend considering a steepened cut slope with
slope stabilization ground anchors and special erosion control measures at this location
In general we believe that a cut slope inclination of up to about 1H 1V may be
achieved with the provision of special erosion control measures The special erosion
control measure for the steepened cut slope should consist of an anchored wire mesh
with grouted soil anchors Provision of an anchored wire mesh cover over the cut slope
face should assist in the retention of the near surface soil horizon on the steepened cut
slope face We believe that the anchored wire mesh should provide positive erosion
control measures for the steepened cut slope
The anchored wire mesh system is an active slope stabilization system where an
alloyed high tensile steel wire mesh is anchored onto the slope face by applying a
defined torque force in the grouted soil anchors and spike plates The anchored wire
mesh system should be designed to withstand the gravity forces from the near surface
soil horizon to reduce the potential for the soils to move under the anchored wire mesh
system Based on our evaluation we recommend that a 10 foot by 10 foot nail spacing
arranged in a triangular grid pattern with 14 foot deep nails be used for the preliminary
Hawaii California
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
FINAL DESIGN SUBMITTAL
design of the anchored wire mesh system at the project site In general the following
provides a brief outline of the installation process for the anchored wire mesh system
1 Excavate the proposed cut slopes to the design grades The cut slope face
should be firm and free of loose materials prior to the installation of the
grouted anchors
2 Stake out the grouted soil anchors in general accordance with the project
spacing requirements taking into consideration the low spots on the cut
slope face
3 Excavate the dell a small depression at each grouted soil anchor location
for pre tensioning of the anchored wire mesh before drilling the grouted soil
anchors
4 Install the grouted soil anchors anchor heads should not project above the
terrain line or predominant slope line
5 Lay the erosion control matting followed by the steel wire mesh panels on
the prepared cut slope face with the installed grouted soil anchors
6 Join or seam the steel wire mesh panels together as needed
7 Fit the boundary wire ropes around the perimeter of the anchored wire mesh
system to provide a neat edge
8 Install the spike plates and pre tension with a torque wrench or hydraulic
press to the specified torque and or force
9 Hydromulch and or seed all exposed cut slope areas after the anchored wire
mesh installation
As mentioned previously the grouted soil anchors should be a minimum of
14 feet long and should be spaced at 10 feet on center in a staggered pattern The
drilled hole for the grouted soil anchor should be a minimum of 4 inches in diameter
The grout and or epoxy resin should be non shrink and should have a minimum
unconfined compressive strength of 4 000 pounds per square inch psi or greater In
addition the grouted soil anchors should have an allowable pullout capacity of 10 kips
with a safety factor of 2 0
Due to the potentially corrosive environment at the project site the draped wire
mesh and hardware should be corrosion resistant Therefore we propose that the
W O 3869 20 A GEOLABS INC Page 59
Hawaii California
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
FINAL DESIGN SUBMITTAL
anchored wire mesh system and hardware be galvanized as a minimum or the entire
system should be made of stainless steel It should be noted that the typical anchored
wire mesh system is galvanized with a zinc aluminum coating for corrosion protection In
addition the wire mesh should be colored to approximate the general coloration of the
natural slope We recommend that the anchored wire mesh system and all associated
hardware such as the high strength steel wire mesh compression claws and spike
plates be powder coated with a black pigment or any available color desired by the State
3 10 Box Culverts and Wing Walls
Based on the information provided we understand that three new box culverts will
be constructed along the proposed alignment for drainage purposes We understand that

of Kaumualii Highway The existing and new box culverts generally are located in the
streams drainageways and marsh lands with potentially soft ground conditions
As previously mentioned due to the potential for ground settlements we
recommend removing the soft soils below the new box culverts Details of the soft soil
over excavation requirements are provided in Soft Ground Stabilization section of this
report
After the over excavation of soft soils the subgrade materials should be scarified
and recompacted to at least 90 percent relative compaction The over excavation should
be backfilled with select granular fill compacted to at least 90 percent relative compaction
In addition a 6 inch gravel cushion layer consisting of open graded gravel AASHTO
M 43 No 67 gradation should be provided below the bottom of the box culvert for
uniform bearing support The granular bedding also should extend beyond the sides of
the box culvert a minimum width of one fourth the outside width of the culvert or
12 inches whichever is greater Where groundwater is encountered a non woven
geotextile fabric Section 716 02 of HSS should wrap around the bedding material and
should extend up the walls of the structure excavation to a level of about 12 inches above
the water level

3 11 Pipe Culverts
In addition to box culverts many pipe culverts of about 18 to 60 inches in diameter
also are planned along the proposed highway widening As mentioned previously where
soft soils are encountered at the inverts of the pipe culverts the soft soils should be
over excavated to expose firm unyielding ground
After over excavation of soft soils where present the subgrade material should be
scarified and re compacted to at least 90 percent relative compaction We recommend
providing granular bedding consisting of 6 inches of gravel cushion AASHTO M 43
No 67 gradation below the pipe culverts for uniform support Free draining granular
materials such as AASHTO M 43 No 67 gradation also should be used for the initial
trench backfill up to about 12 inches above the culverts to provide adequate support
around the pipes The granular bedding should extend beyond the sides of pipes a
W O 3869 20 A GEOLABS INC Page 62
Hawaii California
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
FINAL DESIGN SUBMITTAL
minimum width of one fourth the outside width of the pipes or 12 inches whichever is
greater Where groundwater is encountered a non woven geotextile fabric
Section 716 02 of HSS should wrap around the bedding material and should extend up
the walls of the trench excavation to a level of about 12 inches above the groundwater
level
It is critical to use this free draining material to reduce the potential for formation of
voids below the haunches of pipes and to provide adequate support for the sides of the
pipes Improper trench backfill could result in settlement of the backfill and damage to the
pipes The use of sand or S4C as backfill materials around the pipes should be prohibited
due to the potential for migration or loss of fines during heavy rains which may result in
potential ground settlement and pavement distress
The upper portion of the trench backfill from the level 12 inches above the pipes to
the top of the subgrade or finished grade may consist of on site materials generally less
than 3 inches in maximum size The backfill material should be moisture conditioned to
above the optinum moisture placed in maximum 8 inch level loose lifts and mechanically
compacted to not less than 90 percent relative compaction Where trenches are below
pavement areas the upper 3 feet of the trench backfill below the pavement subgrade
should be compacted to at least 95 percent relative compaction

3 14 Shoring
We anticipate that temporary excavations may be required for construction of the
bridge foundations and culverts Open cut excavation may be desirable in shallow
excavations such as the pier footing excavations provided that the excavation may be set
back away from existing on grade and below grade structures and utility lines Based on
the boring information we believe that temporary cut slopes on the order of about 1H 1V
or flatter may be used for open cut excavations in the medium stiff to very stiff silty soils
anticipated at the project site Excavated soils should not be stockpiled closer than a
horizontal distance equal to the depth of the excavation from the edge of the excavation to
reduce the potential for excessive ground movement
We envision that open cut excavations may not be practical for the installation of
some box culverts and bridge abutments Therefore these excavations will need to be
adequately shored Some of the possible shoring methods include a soldier pile and
lagging shoring system and or sheet piles The excavation support and shoring system
used must comply with applicable safety requirements and the adequacy and safety of
the shoring installation should be made the sole responsibility of the contractor His her
representative who should be required to be continuously present on site during
excavation and construction work will have the best opportunity to promptly observe
changing conditions during construction such as unforeseen subsurface conditions
unexpectedly high groundwater table inappropriate construction sequence or techniques
etc which may affect the shoring stability
In general some minor movements of the shoring system and the adjacent ground
may still occur due to changes in earth stresses during excavation Due to the complexity
of the stress changes it is difficult to accurately estimate the magnitude of movement
The magnitude also depends greatly upon workmanship such as how quickly and tightly
the shoring and bracing supports are installed on the subsurface conditions the size of
the excavation and the rate of excavation Therefore it is important to realize that the
excavation shoring should be installed properly and as early as practical if necessary and
that the adjacent ground should be continuously monitored for cracks dips and or other
indications of movements with instruments The contractor should retain a qualified
W O 3869 20 A GEOLABS INC Page 66
Hawaii California
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
FINAL DESIGN SUBMITTAL
geotechnical engineer and a structural engineer to design and evaluate the shoring
system used
Dewatering of excavations may be necessary where the existing groundwater level
is above the bottom of the proposed excavation Foundation cap excavations for the
Lihue Mill Bridge may encounter groundwater In addition over excavation under box
culverts may also encounter groundwater Therefore dewatering provisions will need to
be included in the contract documents for the proposed construction Because the
excavation will involve discharge of groundwater a National Pollutant Discharge
Elimination System NPDES permit will be required for this discharge The contractor
should consult their independent consultant for the latest regulations and information
pertaining to the permit application
The contractor should be solely responsible for dewatering for construction and
disposal of the dewatered effluent where required The selection of equipment and
methods of dewatering should be left up to the contractor and he she should be aware
that modifications to the dewatering system may be required during construction
depending on the conditions encountered The dewatering method selected should have
minimal impact on the groundwater level surrounding the proposed excavation The
dewatering operations should be coordinated with the trench shoring support such that
the stability of the excavations is not jeopardized The operations should be carried out
without softening the bottom of the excavations
It is our opinion that the definition of Dewatering in the contract documents
should be written to include all works or systems required to lower the natural
groundwater table and or to exclude water from the excavations to allow construction of
the proposed structures under dry and safe conditions These works or systems may
include but are not limited to pumping

3 16 Corrosion Potential
Corrosivity tests consisting of pH minimum resistivity chloride content and
sulfate content tests were performed on the near surface materials at the project site
Results of the corrosivity tests are presented on Plate C 47 in Appendix C Based on the
minimum resistivity value of 3 470 ohm cm which corresponds to Corrosion Rating No 3
according to the guidelines provided by the City and County of Honolulu Board of Water
Supply the near surface soils may be classified as corrosive Design of metallic
substructures such as water line pipes or other metallic piping should consider the
effects of the corrosive environment on the substructure
3 17 Design Review
Final drawings and specifications for the proposed construction should be
forwarded to Geolabs for review and written comments prior to advertisement for bids
This review is necessary to evaluate adherence of the plans and specifications with the
intent of the foundation and earthwork recommendations provided herein If this review is
not made Geolabs cannot assume _ responsibility for misinterpretation of the
recommendations presented in this report
3 18 Post Design Services Services During Construction
It is highly recommended that Geolabs be retained to provide geotechnical
engineering support and continued services during construction of the proposed project
The critical items of construction monitoring that require Special Inspection for this
project include the following
Observation of the subgrade soil preparation
Observation of soft soils over excavation
Observation of fill placement and compaction
Evaluation of the settlement monitoring program
Observation of the trial shaft installation
Observation of the load test shaft installation and load testing
Observation of the production drilled shaft installation
Observation of the micropile load testing
Observation of the production micropile installation
Observation of the micropile proof testing
Observation of the retaining wall foundation excavations

SECTION 4 0 LIMITATIONS
The analyses and recommendations submitted in this report are based in part upon
information obtained from field borings and a review of previous borings performed for the
initial design of this portion of the highway Variations of conditions between and beyond
the field borings may occur and the nature and extent of these variations may not become
evident until construction is underway If variations then appear evident it will be
necessary to re evaluate the recommendations presented in this report
The boring locations indicated in this report are approximate having been
estimated by taping from visible features shown on the plans provided by
Park Engineering on Elevations of the borings were interpolated based
on the contours and spot elevations shown on the same topographic maps The locations
and elevations of the field borings should be considered accurate only to the degree
implied by the methods used
The stratification breaks shown on the graphic representations of the borings depict
the approximate boundaries between soil rock types and as such may denote a gradual
transition Water level data from the borings were measured at the times shown on the
graphic representations and or presented in the text of this report These data have been
reviewed and interpretations made in the formulation of this report It should be noted that
groundwater was not encountered in some of the borings at the time of our field
exploration However it must be noted that fluctuation may occur due to variation in
rainfall perched groundwater conditions stream water level and other factors
This report has been prepared for the exclusive use of Park
Engineering and their client State of Hawaii Department of Transportation Highways
Division for specific application to the Kaumualii Highway Widening Phase 1A project in
accordance with generally accepted geotechnical engineering principles and practices
No warranty is expressed or implied

Hawaii California
SECTION 4 LIMITATIONS
FINAL DESIGN SUBMITTAL
This report has been prepared solely for the purpose of assisting the engineers in
the preparation of the design for the highway widening project Therefore this report may
not contain sufficient data or the proper information for use to form the basis for
preparation of construction cost estimates or contract bidding A contractor wishing to bid
on this project should retain a competent geotechnical engineer to assist in the
interpretation of this report and or performance of site specific exploration for bid
estimating purposes
The owner client should be aware that unanticipated soil conditions are commonly
encountered Unforeseen soil conditions such as perched groundwater soft deposits
hard layers or cavities may occur in localized areas and may require additional probing or
corrections in the field which may result in construction delays to attain a properly
constructed project Therefore a sufficient contingency fund is recommended to
accommodate these possible extra costs
This geotechnical engineering exploration conducted at the project site was not
intended to investigate the potential presence of hazardous materials existing at the
project site It should be noted that the equipment techniques and personnel used to
conduct a geo environmental exploration differ substantially from those applied in
geotechnical engineering

APPENDIX A
Field Exploration and Logs of Borings
FINAL DESIGN SUBMITTAL
APPENDIX A
Field Exploration
The subsurface conditions at the project site Phase 1 were explored by drilling
and sampling 47 borings designated as Boring Nos 101 through 147 extending to depths
of approximately 21 to 102 feet below the existing ground surface The borings were
drilled using a truck mounted and portable drill rig equipped with continuous flight augers
casings and coring tools The approximate boring locations are shown on the Site Plans
Plates 3 1 through 3 13 Details of boring locations and the boring depths are summarized
in Table A 1
The materials encountered in the borings were classified by visual and textural
examination in the field by a geologist who monitored the drilling operations on a
near continuous basis These classifications were further reviewed visually and by testing
in the laboratory Soils were classified in general conformance with the Unified Soil
Classification System as shown on Plate A Graphic representations of the materials
encountered are provided on the Logs of Borings Plates A 1 through A 47
Relatively undisturbed soil samples were obtained from the borings drilled in
general accordance with ASTM D 3550 Ring Lined Barrel Sampling of Soils by driving a
3 inch OD Modified California sampler with a 140 pound hammer falling 30 inches Some
samples were obtained from the drilled borings in general accordance with
ASTM D 1586 Penetration Test and Split Barrel Sampling of Soils by driving a 2 inch
OD standard penetration sampler using the same hammer and drop The blow counts
needed to drive the sampler the second and third 6 inches of an 18 inch drive are shown
as the Penetration Resistance on the Logs of Boring at the appropriate sample depths
Relatively undisturbed samples of the soft soil formation were obtained by pushing a
3 inch OD thin walled stainless steel Shelby tube into the soil formation
Pocket penetrometer and torvane shear tests were performed on selected
cohesive soil samples retrieved in the field The pocket penetrometer test provides an
indication of the unconfined compressive strength of the soil sample The torvane shear
test provided a quick estimate of the undrained shear strength of the soil sample
Pocket penetrometer and torvane shear test results are presented on the Logs of
Borings at the appropriate sample depths and are summarized in Tables C 1 1 through
C 1 14
W O Page A 1
Hawaii California
Appendix A
Field Exploration
FINAL DESIGN SUBMITTAL
Core samples of the rock formations encountered at the site were obtained using
diamond core drilling techniques in general accordance with ASTM Standard Practice
D 2113 Diamond Core Drilling for Site Investigation Core drilling is a rotary drilling
method that uses a hollow bit to cut into the rock formation The material left in the hollow
core of the bit is mechanically recovered for examination and description
Recovery REC is used as a subjective guide to the interpretation of the relative
quality of rock masses Recovery is defined as the actual length of material recovered
from a coring attempt versus the length of the core attempt For example if 3 7 feet of
material is recovered from a 5 0 foot core run the recovery would be 74 percent and
would be shown on the Logs of Borings as REC 74
The Rock Quality Designation RQD is also a subjective guide to the relative
quality of rock masses RQD is defined as the percentage of the core run that is sound
material in excess of 4 inches in length without discontinuities discounting drilling induced
fractures or breaks If 2 5 feet of sound material is recovered from a 5 0 foot core run the
RQ D would be 50 percent and would be shown on the Logs of Borings as RQD 50
Generally the following is used to describe the relative quality of the rock based on the
Practical Handbook of Physical Properties of Rocks and Minerals
Rock Quality RQD
Very Poor 0 25
Poor 25 50
Fair
Good 75 90
Excellent 90 100
The rippability of a rock mass is a function of the relative hardness of the rock its
relative quality brittleness and fissile characteristics A dense basalt formation with a high
RQD values would be very difficult to rip and would probably require more arduous
methods of excavation

APPENDIX B
Previous Exploration
A total of 29 borings designated as Boring Nos 1 through 29 extending to depths
of approximately 19 5 to 102 5 feet below the existing ground surface were drilled for the
report entitled Preliminary Geotechnical Engineering Exploration Preliminary Engineering
Environmental Assessment Kaumualii Highway Widening Lihue to West of Maluhia
Road Island of Kauai Hawaii dated The logs of borings previously
drilled for the above report are provided on Plates B 1 through B 29 for reference It should
be noted that only 13 of the 29 borings previously drilled for the preliminary engineering
phase of the project lies within the Phase 1 alignment The approximate locations of the

APPENDIX C
Laboratory Testing and Laboratory Test Data
FINAL DESIGN SUBMITTAL
APPENDIX C
Laboratory Testing
Moisture Content ASTM D 2216 and Unit Weight ASTM D 2937 determinations
were performed on selected soil samples as an aid in the classification and evaluation of
soil properties The test results are presented on the Logs of Borings at the appropriate
Four Organic Content tests ASTM D 2974 were performed on selected soil
samples to evaluate the amount of organics in the soil and to aid in soil classification The
Twenty six Atterberg Limits tests ASTM D 4318 were performed on selected soil
samples to evaluate the liquid and plastic limits and to aid in soil classification The test
results are summarized on the Logs of Borings at the appropriate sample depths Graphic
presentations of the test results are provided on Plates C 2 through C 4 and are
Five Sieve Analysis tests ASTM C 117 and C 136 were performed on selected
materials encountered in the borings to evaluate the gradation characteristics of the
soils and to aid in soil classification Graphic presentations of the grain size distribution
Five strained controlled consolidated drained Direct Shear tests ASTM D 3080
were performed on selected in situ and remolded soil samples to evaluate the shear
strength characteristics of the in situ soils and remolded soils as fill materials The test
results are presented on Plates C 6 through C 10 and are summarized on Tables C 2
Two Unconsolidated Undrained Triaxial Compression TXUU tests
ASTM D 2850 were performed on selected soil samples to evaluate the undrained
shear strength of the silty and clayey soils encountered The approximate in situ
effective overburden pressure was used as the applied confining pressure for the
relatively undisturbed soil sample The test results and the stress strain curves are
presented on Plates C 11 and C 12 The test results are summarized on Tables C 2
Nine consolidated undrained triaxial compression TXCU tests were performed on
in situ soil samples The tests were performed in accordance with ASTM Test
Designation D 4767 The test results and stress strain curves are presented on
Hawaii California
Appendix C
Laboratory Testing
FINAL DESIGN SUBMITTAL
Twelve Unconfined Compression tests ASTM D 2938 were performed on the
selected core samples to evaluate the unconfined compressive strength of the
weathered basalt rock The test results are summarized on Plate C 20
Nine consolidation tests ASTM D 2435 were performed on selected soft to stiff
silty and clayey soil samples to evaluate the compressibility characteristics of the on site
compressible soils The test results are presented on Plates C 21 through C 29 and are
summarized on Table C 3
Three laboratory Resistance Value tests AASHTO T 190 were performed on
selected bulk samples of the near surface soils to evaluate the pavement support
characteristic of the soils The test results are presented on Plates C 30 through C 32 and
are summarized on Table C 4
Eight laboratory California Bearing Ratio tests ASTM D 1883 were performed on
selected bulk samples of the near surface soils to evaluate the pavement support
characteristics of the soils Three of the eight tests consisted of the modified Kentucky
method The test results are presented on Plates C 33 through C 40 and are
summarized on Table C 4
Three Modified Proctor compaction tests ASTM D 1557 and three Standard
Proctor compaction tests ASTM D 698 were performed on selected bulk samples
obtained to evaluate the relationship between the moisture content and the dry density of
the near surface soils as fill materials The test results are presented on Plates C 41
through C 46 and are summarized on Table C 4
Seven sets of corrosivity tests consisting of minimum resistivity
chloride content and sulfate content tests were
performed on selected soil samples obtained from our field exploration The test results
are presented on Plate C 47

Previous Laboratory Testing

for the above report are provided on Plates D 1 through D 47 for reference
